< Text>
I drive by here on the way to work almost daily, today I saw that their sign said PUPUSAS so I turned around and decided to give then a try.

I called ahead and ordered the chicharron con queso, didnt ask for price. When I got there and saw the menu, I noticed they were $5 each which seemed awfully steep.

The pupusas were large and flat, unlike authentic pupusas. These were more like quesadillas. The pork was not mixed like typical Salvadorean "chicharron" and there wasn't much filling, I honestly dont think there was cheese in mine.

The curtido and salsa were even more disappointing. I got green salsa and some weird looking guacamole sauce...are these people even Salvadorean? Ever eat a pupusa? Such a disgrace to my people.<//Text>

<rating>3</rating><text>For the price you can't complain, big portions  around 8 bucks for the flour veggie tortillas which I recommend. Service is friendly.  They do sauces which are hot (green) but the person serving should remind people (and I spoke Spanish) to pick them up.

I really wanted to give a five, but after the first time the quality of serving dropped (no sour cream served on the 3rd visit, lettuce was a bit too thick and needed to be chopped finer). Only when I asked for sauce was it offered. Small things but it'd  make a stranger give them the most.

The quesdillas are very nice, the onion is a great accompaniment and which makes it over the plain ones. I think the guacamole and sour cream serving is small. I just about put it in 2. In 4, no way. I say make an option pay a dollar more and get more of both.</text>< Pics>

<Text>I was bummed! I had a bad experience from beginning to end. I called ahead of time to see if they had wireless Internet as I had to get some work done while I had food. They said they did so off I went in search of "Aromas." I showed up and every table near the front of the cafe and near any windows said "Reserved for 2 or more people!" How lame is that? I had to sit in the back of the restaurant away from all of the light and all the people. LAME. But I toughed it out and found a table in the back. I unloaded my lapto, plugged in and turned on. Then I made my way to the front counter. I proceeded to order some breakfast and coffee. I went to hand them my credit card and BAM..... they only take cash. The guy behind the counter pointed at a TINY little sign on the register that said "cash only." He pointed to an ATM machine about 10 feet away. THAT SUCKS! I had to get out of line. I took out cash which cost me $1.75 at the ATM and another $2.00 from Wells Fargo! I had to pay $3.75 to pay the guy $8.00! How lame is that! So I went and got back in line. I finished paying and went to sit down. then I decided to trek across the cafe to the bathroom to find that it's controlled by a key. The sign said go ask the kitchen for the key. I went to the kitchen and asked for the key. The guy pointed to a key back towards the bathroom and seemed annoyed that I didn't see it. LAME AGAIN! So after the bathroom I logged on to my computer and guess what..... the wireless takes a "key." Back to line for a third time I go. I got to the front of the line and got the code. I got back to my table and guess what.... the Internet wouldn't work. So the bottom line:
1. What cafe doesn't take plastic?!? What are they stuck in the stone ages?
2. The Internet access sucks! There's a Starbucks 3 doors down that has great WiFi.
3. The bathroom key is in the middle of the restaurant so don't do what the sign says and just look for the key under a hanging arrow.
4. They make you sit in the back if you're by yourself. Bring a friend to be disappointed with. At least that way you might get to sit where it's actually light.

The coffee was pretty good. The food was okay.  The hassle was huge and I HATE having to spend money in fees just to pay for a lazy company that doesn't want to take plastic.

Bottom Line: LAME, UNFRIENDLY and stuck in the stone ages.<//Text>< Pics>

<rating>2<//rating>< Review>
I was bummed! I had a bad experience from beginning to end. I called ahead of time to see if they had wireless Internet as I had to get some work done while I had food. They said they did so off I went in search of "Aromas." I showed up and every table near the front of the cafe and near any windows said "Reserved for 2 or more people!" How lame is that? I had to sit in the back of the restaurant away from all of the light and all the people. LAME. But I toughed it out and found a table in the back. I unloaded my lapto, plugged in and turned on. Then I made my way to the front counter. I proceeded to order some breakfast and coffee. I went to hand them my credit card and BAM..... they only take cash. The guy behind the counter pointed at a TINY little sign on the register that said "cash only." He pointed to an ATM machine about 10 feet away. THAT SUCKS! I had to get out of line. I took out cash which cost me $1.75 at the ATM and another $2.00 from Wells Fargo! I had to pay $3.75 to pay the guy $8.00! How lame is that! So I went and got back in line. I finished paying and went to sit down. then I decided to trek across the cafe to the bathroom to find that it's controlled by a key. The sign said go ask the kitchen for the key. I went to the kitchen and asked for the key. The guy pointed to a key back towards the bathroom and seemed annoyed that I didn't see it. LAME AGAIN! So after the bathroom I logged on to my computer and guess what..... the wireless takes a "key." Back to line for a third time I go. I got to the front of the line and got the code. I got back to my table and guess what.... the Internet wouldn't work. So the bottom line:
1. What cafe doesn't take plastic?!? What are they stuck in the stone ages?
2. The Internet access sucks! There's a Starbucks 3 doors down that has great WiFi.
3. The bathroom key is in the middle of the restaurant so don't do what the sign says and just look for the key under a hanging arrow.
4. They make you sit in the back if you're by yourself. Bring a friend to be disappointed with. At least that way you might get to sit where it's actually light.

The coffee was pretty good. The food was okay.  The hassle was huge and I HATE having to spend money in fees just to pay for a lazy company that doesn't want to take plastic.

Bottom Line: LAME, UNFRIENDLY and stuck in the stone ages.</Review>

<Resp>None<//Resp>< text>
I had a wash done on my RAV4 SUV here... it looked good so I tipped the guy and went on my merry way. However later on after I got home I noticed that the top wasn't completely washed in places underneath the cross bars. My car wasn't very dirty other than it had a layer of ashes from the fires and dust on it. In case you are not  aware wood ash from the wildfires can cause paint damage to your vehicle if not rinsed off thoroughly AND washed with soapy water then rinsed and dried. If you just rinse it off and leave it then you will probably end up having paint damage. Wood ash mixed with water is how lye is made and lye is acidic. I called and spoke to the owner David who was very cordial and told him of the fact that my vehicle's top wasn't properly cleaned. He asked me to bring the car back  in and explained how the automated wash worked and that although the top was actually washed that the brushes can't get underneath cross bars. However it should be cleaned by the guy that finishes and wipes your car down. So he had a guy clean the roof properly. Thank you Dave, I will be taking my car back for claying and waxing, etc.</text>

<username>Chad Todd< /username><date>1611607412828< /date><Rate>5</Rate>< Review>
I cannot believe the negative reviews. Most of them seem to be disgruntled people in general. My experience with Alex and his team has been great. He replaced a motor for me in my 2012 Toyota Prius, and the change went smoothly, for a very reasonable cost, considering the work being done. The engine has a 6 month warranty on it, and at the 3 month mark it start knocking in the motor. I took it back, fearing the worst. After all I had a used motor put in the car, and that carries some risk with it naturally. Alex's team looked at it and determined it was the lifters knocking. They saw the car was throwing a code for a bad sensor. They changed that sensor, replaced the oil, and the knocking went away. I still have 3 months left on the engine warranty too. They were fair about the cost for this and I am very happy with their service. Highly recommended.

The only knock I have is both times I have taken my car in I noticed grease on the door handle and center console where your arm would rest while driving the car. I cleaned this off as it isn't that big a deal and not enough to knock off a star, but would be nice to have the grease cleaned off or have the mechanics wear gloves in the car. Also, they are very very busy so there can sometimes be a wait, but that just shows they know their stuff and they are in demand.</Review>

< Review>
I was recommended this place by friends brother-in-law as a shop that does excellent work at a good price. I took my 86 4runner to P&G Auto for an engine swap (22rec). Please make no mistake, Alex and everyone who works there was very polite and awesome. There is a starting point to consider as well in this review and that is that this motor ran even with a cracked block, I started to remove the valve covers and discovered the crack, at that point took it to P&G. Alex quoted me with an extremely fair price of $1400 with a $700 deposit to start work. After 2 weeks or less I got the call that it would be ready. I took the day off work, and got a ride to Rialto. Waited approx 4 hours and then Alex informed me that it wouldn't be ready that day. No problem, a few more days go by and I get the call that it will be done and ready to pick-up Thursday. Take the day off work, get a ride to Rialto, watched in the shop (I was told it was an open shop and customers may watch) as two different mechanics try to assemble the EFI to the head. First one declared it good as the motor started and I pointed out to him that a considerable amount of gas was leaking out of the bottom of the fuel rail assembly. This repeated twice as the O-rings kept getting pinched from incorrect installation. I was then asked to go wait back upfront because the mechanic was nervous with me watching over his shoulder. Totally understandable, I can be the same way at my job. After 2 more hours, they come upfront and tell me that it won't be ready that day either. I get a call the next week and Alex said they got it running and took it for a test drive and the brakes are bad and the wheel cylinders,master cylinder, and calipers need to be replaced. Ok too the first two, I'll wait on the calipers. Then the fuel pump and alternator were bad. Ok replace those after all they are prob over 20 years old no problem. Get the third call that it will be ready. Leave work early, get a ride to Rialto. Fuel pump STAR AUTO PARTS delivered was a dud. No worries guy is on his way with a new one, no charge, and heres a free star auto parts sweater. Ok I love free stuff. 2 hours and the fuel pump is in, test drive and the idle is a little out of wack, no worries, adjusted the idle and took the truck home. So with understanding to it being an old truck, and more things went wrong than were known the $1400 estimate went to $2750. Ouch but I was glad to have the truck back, I love my Yota. Less than a week out the fuel pump fails on the freeway. P&G brought a tow truck and grabbed me off the 210, much appreciated no cost to me.
This was a year ago and this is where its at now. 2 of the four injectors installed turned out to be used (not rebuilt cores, used). Many of the parts installed on the motor were used and rusted, painted over with black paint which has now peeled. The motor was assembled without the throttle position sensor, the new radiator sprung a leak, alternator will be replaced shortly since when I turn on the headlights the idle drops and the motor sputters. Replacing the fuel pump on principle alone (never buy star auto parts pumps), I just went to replace the header and only two stock studs were there (supposed to be all studs), the rest were bolts, 2 of the bolts were stripped and now I have to re-tap the head.
So is the motor running? barely but it is running. Is P&G all to blame? Absolutely not, some of the sensors and what not could have been damaged when I took it in. However, at the end of the day this is what I take inventory on; I lost 2 days of pay (about $300 wages before taxes) not counting the 1/2 day to pick it up when it was finally ready and asking for rides from work in orange county to Rialto. I have a stripped head bolts, used parts, and a motor that still does not run correct. All for a total cost of about $3000 including time lost, not including personal headache and zero confidence in the motors assembly.</Review>

<rating>3< /rating>< review>
I've brought my Chiweenie Duke to this Petsmart location twice now for a "Brush and Bath" package and each time the experience has been alright, but a couple of questionable things have come up that might make me think twice about returning ever again.

On this go-around, when I arrived, the curb-side pick-up situation was completely unorganized and chaotic. Customers didn't know where to go, who was next, what employee was available...it was a complete mess.  Joceline was my groomer and she was nice and all, but very robotic and not personable at all.

Joceline rushed me through the signing of the paperwork and the initial inspection of my dog that is supposed to happen when you drop your pet off never was mentioned and never happened.  She asked me to remove his collar (which I was not asked to do the previous time I brought him in, so it made me kinda uncomfortable doing this) and his harness so she could put this red leash around his neck to take him inside (also didn't happen the first time I brought him in and made me feel not too keen about leaving him there).

I asked Joceline how long the appointment would take and she advised me 3-4 hours, yet my dog was ready 1.5 hours later.  And, when I came to pick-up Duke he was just handed off to me....that's it. I didn't get a "Pawgress Report" as I did before about how the appointment went and when she saw me while bringing out another dog to its owner, she asked if I had paid yet and I said I hadn't.  She advised me to get into this extremely long line of customers to pay for his appointment or go online and pay through the app.  Since there was 1 employee and 10 customers waiting to check out, I chose to pay on the app.  It was a process because I had to add my credit card and all that, but had I been advised that I could pay in advance by Joceline when I dropped him off, then I would have had the appointment paid in full before I got there to pick him up.  When she came back out with Duke, she did not ask for proof of payment or anything, she just took the red leash off around his neck and went to go get the next pet to bring in.

My dog is basically my child, so when he is treated like a number and the customer service is bleak, it kinda leaves a bad taste in my mouth about the business.  And if you offer certain services online and through the marketing campaigns you send in your emails, you should provide those services or advised the customer you cannot provide them and the reason why.

All in all, I was not too impressed the 2nd time around and most likely will look for either another PetSmart grooming location near me or another business altogether.  Based on the Yelp reviews for the surrounding PetSmart's though, it looks like I will be looking for another grooming business altogether.</review>

< Review>
Pet Hotel - I do not recommend.
I never do reviews but felt this one was important.  Wish I could say this was great experience, however from the time we arrived to now as I am writing this post, I cannot recommend the Canoga Park location.

First, when we arrived, the staff was not friendly and do not know how to deliver a pleasant message regarding all the "policies" about a pet staying at their hotel.  I rented a suite for my 2 dogs, and they have strict rules that each dog can only have one personal item.  Ok, whatever.

We paid for camp days, along with the suite because we do spoil our fur babies .  I made sure they had their own food, treats etc.

Every time I would call to check in, I would be put on hold several times before someone would actually get on the line from the pet hotel.  The last call the store manager finally helped me...this took over 25 minute, but I did appreciate that she made the effort.

When we picked them up they were just "off".  Physically and emotionally. Both dogs were upset, and just wanted to get out.  One of my dogs cried all the way home.  I just chalked I up to the fact we rarely board our dogs, and they would settle back in.  However, this really was not the case.

One of dogs had major diarrhea that lasted about a week. Not sure if they even fed our food to them or some other food they are not used to.

Also, one of dogs had to be taken into the vet for leg injury within about 2 days of picking her up.  This cost me $130, but thankfully nothing major.  I can't say for sure how this my have happened, but it was coincidental with the stay.

Approximately 10 days later, one of my dogs developed kennel cough.  Our dogs are not exposed to other dogs, other than when they were boarded. So, now we are dealing with this.

All this said, I did have great experience at the Northridge location.  Unfortunately, they did not have a suite available wen we needed to book for our trip.

Hope I helps other dog owners when deciding on where to board there pets.  I know we will not be returning to the Conga Park location.< /Review>

I really like going to this PetSmart even though it isn't the closest PetSmart to me I go out of my way and travel a bit more to go to this one.
